  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6bda912a-6770-4c93-aecb-9d5bbca89e0d'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer625497412031862851">Blue Echohawk doesn't know who she is. She doesn't know her real name or when she was born. Abandoned at two and raised by a drifter, she didn't attend school until she was ten years old. At nineteen, when most kids her age are attending college or moving on with life, she is just a senior in high school. With no mother, no father, no faith, and no future, Blue Echohawk is</span>
  <span id="freeText625497412031862851" style="display:none">Blue Echohawk doesn't know who she is. She doesn't know her real name or when she was born. Abandoned at two and raised by a drifter, she didn't attend school until she was ten years old. At nineteen, when most kids her age are attending college or moving on with life, she is just a senior in high school. With no mother, no father, no faith, and no future, Blue Echohawk is a difficult student, to say the least. Tough, hard and overtly sexy, she is the complete opposite of the young British teacher who decides he is up for the challenge, and takes the troublemaker under his wing. <br /><br />This is the story of a nobody who becomes somebody. It is the story of an unlikely friendship, where hope fosters healing and redemption becomes love. But falling in love can be hard when you don't know who you are. Falling in love with someone who knows exactly who they are and exactly why they can't love you back might be impossible.</span>
  <a data-text-id="625497412031862851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1119337-in-the-book-blue-one-time-uses-a-british">In the book Blue one time uses a British expression, saying something around the lines of &quot;I&#39;m feeling knackered or was it knickered?&quot; to which Wilson responds that she certainly ain&#39;t &quot;knickered&quot;. Blue made a mental note in the book that she needed to look it up, but unfortunately never does.
So is there a &quot;knickered&quot;? And what is it supposed to mean then?</a>
</div>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/197236-the-timeline-for-this-book-really-pulls-me">The timeline for this book really pulls me out of the story. The years given are August 1993, September and October 2010, and March 2012.

The plot doesn&#39;t allow a 1 year time jump, but ages going forward follow the mistake. Anyone else notice this? Have a solution?

I can&#39;t easily correct the mistake one way or another in my head. 2010 to 2011 causes problems. 2012 to 2011 causes other problems.</a>
</div>

It said she started her senior year in September 2010 and then it went to like March 2012. It confused me too. Plus when it dated on her per sample. I was like how did we skip a year.   <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415601i/820429.jpg' alt=' photo 317a634f-3c6e-488d-88db-b1ca0b1f6633_zpsbf7d14a5.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>5 'Different' Stars</b><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/fd412149-3431-4aee-935a-236b1a3d860d_zps90803765.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415601i/820430.jpg' alt=' photo fd412149-3431-4aee-935a-236b1a3d860d_zps90803765.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Who is Blue Echohawk? Even she doesn’t know. Blue is not her real name, she's not sure what that is. She thinks she is 19 or maybe 20, she's not sure. Blue was left with a stranger, Jimmy Echohawk when she was around 2 years old. Her mother abandoned her and was found dead later. Jimmy raised her as his own, but after Jimmy died, Blue had no one. She doesn't know who she is. The first day of her senior year of high school, she will meet someone who will change her. Who</span>
  <span id="freeText11719812770415672080" style="display:none"><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/317a634f-3c6e-488d-88db-b1ca0b1f6633_zpsbf7d14a5.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415601i/820429.jpg" alt=" photo 317a634f-3c6e-488d-88db-b1ca0b1f6633_zpsbf7d14a5.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>5 'Different' Stars</b><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/fd412149-3431-4aee-935a-236b1a3d860d_zps90803765.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415601i/820430.jpg" alt=" photo fd412149-3431-4aee-935a-236b1a3d860d_zps90803765.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Who is Blue Echohawk? Even she doesn’t know. Blue is not her real name, she's not sure what that is. She thinks she is 19 or maybe 20, she's not sure. Blue was left with a stranger, Jimmy Echohawk when she was around 2 years old. Her mother abandoned her and was found dead later. Jimmy raised her as his own, but after Jimmy died, Blue had no one. She doesn't know who she is. The first day of her senior year of high school, she will meet someone who will change her. Who helps her find herself. Her history teacher, Mr. Wilson.<br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/6bbaf482-4bf4-4c50-a5fc-0fcf7f75ee86_zpsc64b2639.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415601i/820431.jpg" alt=" photo 6bbaf482-4bf4-4c50-a5fc-0fcf7f75ee86_zpsc64b2639.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Why don’t you focus more on where you’re going and less on where you came from? Why don’t you focus more on what makes you brilliant and less on what makes you angry?”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Mr. Darcy Wilson is british and he is a young guy- only a few years older than Blue. He moved to the state several years ago, and this is his first year teaching. Even though Blue keeps her distance from pretty much everyone, a string of events bring these two closer together and they develop an unlikely friendship. The lessons in Wilson’s class really speak to Blue and inspires her art. <br><b>
  <blockquote>‘Life is all we have, and we live it as we believe in living it. But to sacrifice what you are and to live without belief, that is a fate more terrible than dying.’</blockquote>
</b><br>Blue is trying to find herself. She isn’t happy with the path she is on. When she finally tries to change it, things happen that make it even more difficult. She feels alone in the world, a nobody. <br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/6f4f4fb1-2ef4-4eb4-bd3a-bd10b75e51ea_zpsb8d14af8.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415601i/820432.jpg" alt=" photo 6f4f4fb1-2ef4-4eb4-bd3a-bd10b75e51ea_zpsb8d14af8.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Wilson makes her feel like a somebody. Though they have chemistry, its just not in the cards for them to be together- even after graduation, Wilson was still Blue’s teacher, and Blue is going through a lot. But Wilson quickly becomes Blue’s best friend. He is there for her through her journey. <br><br>Darcy Wilson... What an amazing man! Caring, supportive, funny, smart- the total package. You will fall in love with his compassionate self, and British accent! <br>Blue was tough, she has had a hard life, but she is a survivor. <br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>“I was scarred, but I was not broken. Beneath my insecurities, beneath my pain, beneath my struggle, beneath it all, I was still whole"</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br>No matter what she went through or what was thrown her way, she kept it together. She was strong, feisty, and I loved how much a smartass she was at the beginning. Her life wasn’t easy, but it was hers. It made her into the beautiful person she became. <br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I keep wishing you had a better life... a different life. But a different life would have made you a different Blue. And that would be the biggest tragedy of all.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>The last few chapters blew me away. It was just incredible when Blue found out about herself and everything became full circle. <br><br>An amazing, heartbreaking story about a girl trying to redeem herself, and finding herself in the process. It was emotinoal and heavy at times, but also sweet and funny. Beautiful and captivating- not one I would pass up. This one comes highly recommended by yours truly! <br><br>My favorite line:<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Girls like me notice guys like you. We just don’t think we deserve them.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/89f36500-27ee-4cfc-a257-ffda31166a04_zps8a0fac0d.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415601i/820433.jpg" alt=" photo 89f36500-27ee-4cfc-a257-ffda31166a04_zps8a0fac0d.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Once upon a time there was a little bird who was placed into a nest. Wanted. Cherished. Unafraid, because she knew she was a hawk, a beautiful bird, worth of awe, deserving of love...”</blockquote>
</b><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="11719812770415672080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a title="SueBee★bring me an alpha!★" class="user" itemprop="url" name="SueBee★bring me an alpha!★" href="/user/show/15735368-suebee-bring-me-an-alpha">SueBee★bring me an alpha!★</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17830192-a-different-blue">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer578426616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5683516440576961775"><a href='http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/HarmonAdifferentBlueTitlebySueBee_zpscd804a01.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415907i/821238.jpg' alt=' photo HarmonAdifferentBlueTitlebySueBee_zpscd804a01.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>★★★★★! A different Blue (stand-alone) A poignant & captivating tale about a young girl with no past & no hopes for a future!</b><br/><br/><b><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ynlQ8Oz8Qmk' rel='nofollow noopener'>Click here </a>to hear the song Mr. Wilson played on his cello that brought so much joy to Blue!</b><br/><br/><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“Once upon a time there was a little blackbird who was pushed from the nest, unwanted. Discarded.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br/><b>A Different Blue is an emotional and beautifully told story about a young girl with no history, no self-worth and no future. At least that is how Blue Echohaw</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5683516440576961775" style="display:none"><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/HarmonAdifferentBlueTitlebySueBee_zpscd804a01.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415907i/821238.jpg" alt=" photo HarmonAdifferentBlueTitlebySueBee_zpscd804a01.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>★★★★★! A different Blue (stand-alone) A poignant &amp; captivating tale about a young girl with no past &amp; no hopes for a future!</b><br><br><b><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ynlQ8Oz8Qmk" rel="nofollow noopener">Click here </a>to hear the song Mr. Wilson played on his cello that brought so much joy to Blue!</b><br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“Once upon a time there was a little blackbird who was pushed from the nest, unwanted. Discarded.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br><b>A Different Blue is an emotional and beautifully told story about a young girl with no history, no self-worth and no future. At least that is how Blue Echohawk sees herself</b> when her story opens up on her first day of her senior year in High school. Late for European History class she saunters in and meets her <b>new and very young, handsome, half-British teacher Mr. Wilson</b>.<br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“My job this year is to introduce you to stories that open your mind to a broader world – a colorful history – and to help you see the connections to your own life.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br>The story follows Blue during her <b>last year of high school and beyond</b>. Blue and Mr. Wilson were off a rocky start with a rebellious and despondent Blue fighting him every step of the way. But <b>Mr. Wilson never gives up on Blue and slowly wins her over</b>.<br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“Why don't you focus more on what makes you brilliant and less on what makes you angry? You are missing a key element to the story...”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br>They settle into a mutually respectful teacher-student relationship. Follow them as they have to <b>deal with life’s setbacks, trials and tribulations</b>. As the school year comes to an end the roles switch. In the friendship that ensues <b>the student very much becomes the teacher</b>. <br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“Loving someone means putting their needs above your own. No matter what. Somehow, you figured that out. I'll be damned if I know how, but you did.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br>As a reader it’s clear that they have connection and strong feelings for each other, but <b>Blue doesn’t think she is worthy</b> of Wilson while <b>he feels a moral obligation as her former teacher and elder by 3 years</b>. And while Blue is truly a girl with no past, <b>Wilson has a past to deal with</b>.<br><br><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/HarmonAdifferentBlueHeroinebySueBee_zps72fa5d14.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415907i/821239.jpg" alt=" photo HarmonAdifferentBlueHeroinebySueBee_zps72fa5d14.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Blue Echohawk</b> is an amazing heroine. Imagine knowing you were abandoned and with no knowledge of your past and no real hope for a future. Yet amazingly on her journey she not only finds herself, but she is able to profoundly impact several people’s lives. She will stay with me! Six words to describe <b>Blue: Brilliant, strong, defiant, despondent, captivating and lost</b>.<br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“And in weeping there was power. The power to heal, the power to release pain and let go, the power to endure love and to shoulder loss.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/HarmonAdifferentBlueHerobySueBee_zps56700b59.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415907i/821240.jpg" alt=" photo HarmonAdifferentBlueHerobySueBee_zps56700b59.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Mr. Darcy Wilson, Wilson</b>, the prodigal son of a doctor, graduated University at age nineteen. He refused to follow his father’s foot step an instead became a high school teacher at the tender age of twenty-two. Six words to describe <b>Wilson: Brilliant, nurturing, caring, focused, insightful and noble</b>.<br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“I keep wishing you had had a better life . . . a different life. But a different life would have made you a different Blue.” He looked at me then. “And that would be the biggest tragedy of all.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br><b>A different Blue</b> kept me glued to my Kindle in a way I very rarely do. I needed to see Blue <b>uncovering her past and coming to terms with her future and finding herself</b>. I needed to know more about the <b>enigmatic Wilson to learn what is holding him back</b> and as their romance slowly unfolds I needed to make sure they would find their way to each other. I should not disclose any more. <b>Their story is best experienced!!!</b><br><br><b>Spellbinding storytelling! Beautiful yet heart-wrenching plot! Compelling and unforgettable characters! A captivating and emotional read! Thanks Ms. Harmon!</b><br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“Luckily, the picture wasn't damaged. We were still whole beneath the jagged scar. I stopped, considering. I was scarred, but I was not broken. Beneath my wounds I was still whole. Beneath my insecurities, beneath my pain, beneath my struggle, beneath it all, I was still whole.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br>***<br>Hero rating: 4.5 stars <br>Heroine rating: 5 stars<br>Sex scenes rating: N/A<br>Sex scenes frequency: N/A<br>Storyline concept rating: 5 stars<br>Storyline execution rating: 5 stars<br>Storytelling skills rating: 5 stars<br>Story ending rating: 4.5 stars<br>Book editing rating (5 = no edits spotted): 5 stars<br>************************************************<br><b>Overall rating: 5 stars<br><br>Would I recommend this book: Yes.<br>Would I re-read this book: Probably.<br>Would I read future books by this author: Yes.</b><br><br><a href="http://s1340.photobucket.com/user/smkarl/media/GIF%20hands/tumblr_mg5ruzlkg71qgawlzo1_500_zps94160098.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380415907ra/821241.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mg5ruzlkg71qgawlzo1_500_zps94160098.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5683516440576961775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer587989779" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12335733457791223344"><b>*A story to savor!*</b><br/><br/>Some stories have the power to change us. Whether it's for a lifetime, or just a moment—its effects are undeniable. The moment a book becomes a channel that reaches into the soul of its reader is one of life's sweetest gifts. For me, <i>A Different Blue</i> is one of those gifts. <br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I'm nobody! Who are you? Are you nobody, too?</i>
  </b>
  <br/>
  <i>- Emily Dickinson</i>
</blockquote> <a href='http://tinypic.com?ref=2vrzjao' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img height='420' width='395' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417293i/825174.jpg' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/> <b>Blue Echohawk</b> lives in a lonely world that has beaten down and abandoned her. Wearing an armor of attitude and a mask of </span>
  <span id="freeText12335733457791223344" style="display:none"><b>*A story to savor!*</b><br><br>Some stories have the power to change us. Whether it's for a lifetime, or just a moment—its effects are undeniable. The moment a book becomes a channel that reaches into the soul of its reader is one of life's sweetest gifts. For me, <i>A Different Blue</i> is one of those gifts. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I'm nobody! Who are you? Are you nobody, too?</i>
  </b>
  <br>
  <i>- Emily Dickinson</i>
</blockquote> <a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2vrzjao" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="420" width="395" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417293i/825174.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br> <b>Blue Echohawk</b> lives in a lonely world that has beaten down and abandoned her. Wearing an armor of attitude and a mask of makeup, she faces the world with an intimidating strength which runs only skin deep. Her actions are cold and her words, offensive--but her insides are as weak and fragile as a lost little bird...<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Once upon a time there was a little blackbird who was pushed out of the nest, unwanted. Discarded...</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>Darcy Wilson</b> appears to be everything Blue believes she's not; he's confident, educated, and comes from a loving, happy family. Her mind tells her she'd never be good enough for him, but her heart disagrees. <br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>I wanted to hate him because he was beautiful in a way I would never be.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>Wilson's patient and honorable character moved me, but ultimately, it was Blue's redeeming qualities and quiet strength that stole my heart. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>God? I'm ugly inside. And it's not my fault. You know it's not.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>The engaging writing and realistic dialogue captured me instantly. This story moves at a slow and steady pace, but I felt it was a driving force in getting the messages received. The slow building relationship between Blue and Wilson allows us to focus on the important elements of the plot and I appreciated the healing friendship that evolved beforehand. The gorgeous symbolism is offered delicately, yet made apparent in various ways as long as your mind is left open enough to accept it. <br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=1htnar" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417293i/825175._SX540_.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This unique story is beautiful on a so many levels. The power of literature, music, historical myths and legends forcefully grace these pages and I found so much insight and depth in its wake. There were pivotal moments that inspired chills and brought me to tears by its beauty alone. <br><br>Although this book often displayed a melancholy tone, its messages are uplifting and entirely positive. But even more than that, this story ultimately <b>inspires.</b> It challenges us to not let our pasts dictate our future. To look 'beyond what is obvious' and see 'what is possible'. To take control over our lives and learn from the pain instead of wallowing in the <i>why's</i>...Because, when it comes to pain and heartache, the <i>reasons</i> are never enough to remain forever broken. <br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>There's no sense in running from the past. We can't throw it away or pretend it didn't happen, Miss Echohawk. But maybe we can learn something from it. You have an interesting story, and I'd like you to tell me more...</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=30vc849" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417293i/825176.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br> <a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2mh7uop" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="50" width="50" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347313i/701667.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><b>
  <u>Book Stats:</u>
</b><br><b>▪	 Genre/Category:</b> Romance/New Adult<br><b>▪	 Steam Caliber:</b> Mild/Sexy<br><b>▪ Romance:</b> Very slow build-up. Beautiful connection. <br><b>▪	 Characters:</b> Admirable and sexy hero. Damaged, intriguing, enigmatic heroine. <br><b>▪	 Plot:</b> Slow and steady narrative, with an intense and inspiring tone. <br><b>▪ Writing:</b> Gorgeous! Uplifting and alluring. Captivating execution. <br><b>▪ POV:</b> First person: Heroine<br><b>▪	 Cliffhanger:</b> None/Standalone<br><b>▪ HEA? </b><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Yes <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><a href="http://prettywordsbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412050368i/11316768.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Pretty-Words-Book-Blog/860331017317983" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height='“40"' width="150" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413062455i/11461733._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="12335733457791223344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦" href="/user/show/44673856-maria-steamy-reads-blog">Maria✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1600614510" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15372427637877902484"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463858938i/19168430.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464909548i/19291214._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I'm nobody, who are you? Are you nobody too?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466042213i/19431593.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>➦This stand alone novel by Amy Harmon follows a life of a girl named Blue. Strange name, right? <b>Why was she called blue?</b> All the questions will be answered in this wonderful story of a woman who is on a <b>quest of self-discovery.</b><br/><br/>➦The book begins with showing us Blue as a <b>troubled teenager.</b> Having been abandoned at a very young age, Blue struggles with her identity. Wilson, her <b>high school history teacher</b>, helps Blue express herself through </span>
  <span id="freeText15372427637877902484" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463858938i/19168430.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464909548i/19291214._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I'm nobody, who are you? Are you nobody too?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466042213i/19431593.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>➦This stand alone novel by Amy Harmon follows a life of a girl named Blue. Strange name, right? <b>Why was she called blue?</b> All the questions will be answered in this wonderful story of a woman who is on a <b>quest of self-discovery.</b><br><br>➦The book begins with showing us Blue as a <b>troubled teenager.</b> Having been abandoned at a very young age, Blue struggles with her identity. Wilson, her <b>high school history teacher</b>, helps Blue express herself through woodcarving. Blue is extremely talented but has low self esteem and Wilson plays a huge role in helping her grow her talent. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464912189ra/19291422.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Someone told me once that to create true art you must be willing to bleed and let others watch.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466042213i/19431593.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>➦Blue and Wilson continue their friendship even after high school. She draws inspiration from Wilson's history lessons and later on from his cello playing. Wilson also supports her in her <b>search for her family.</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464912189ra/19291423.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>❤I loved Blue's character. She did make some bad choices but she was able to bounce back and move on. The book has <b>flashbacks into her past</b> and it helped me understand what it was like for her to grow up without really knowing who she was. <br><br>❤This novel has a very <b>romantic</b> tone to it, with frequent <b>references to history and poetry</b>. I found it rather interesting and at times educational. <br><br>➦I would recommend this book to anyone who loves <b>slow burn</b> and <b>"friends first"</b> romances. This was <b>REALLY slow burn</b> so if you are looking for hot and steamy action you won't be finding it here. There's no forbidden love in this one even though these two start out as student and teacher. Fans of <b>Mariana Zapata</b> would probably enjoy this one :)<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1466042213i/19431593.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/SteamyReadsBlog/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473872687i/20525702.jpg" width="40" height="40" alt="Follow us on facebook" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.instagram.com/steamyreads/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473872687i/20525703.jpg" width="40" height="40" alt="Follow us on instagram" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="http://www.steamyreads.net" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473872687i/20525705.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3368146738?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3368146738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7571683512894515419">reading one of an authors first novels, especially after having read their most recent books first, can be tricky. all authors have to start somewhere, so if the writing or story isnt as great as a reader might be used to, it can be difficult to remember to not judge. but i do think its always enlightening to see an authors roots and their beginnings. and i think <i>‘a different blue’</i> does that.<br/><br/>i can see roots of the emotive storytelling that i have to love from AH, but its not quite as developed i</span>
  <span id="freeText7571683512894515419" style="display:none">reading one of an authors first novels, especially after having read their most recent books first, can be tricky. all authors have to start somewhere, so if the writing or story isnt as great as a reader might be used to, it can be difficult to remember to not judge. but i do think its always enlightening to see an authors roots and their beginnings. and i think <i>‘a different blue’</i> does that.<br /><br />i can see roots of the emotive storytelling that i have to love from AH, but its not quite as developed in this particular book. i found the characters to be a little unrelatable, the dialogue not as natural, and the pacing a bit slow. but the writing and overall meaning of the story is as lovely as ever. <br /><br />definitely not AHs strongest story, which makes sense since she has become such an incredible writer over the year, but still enjoyable and worth the read. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_2006997794" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2006997794" />
    <a title="Astrid - The Bookish Sweet Tooth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7420520-astrid---the-bookish-sweet-tooth"><img alt="Astrid - The Bookish Sweet Tooth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558713329p2/7420520.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2006997794?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Astrid - The Bookish Sweet Tooth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Astrid - The Bookish Sweet Tooth" href="/user/show/7420520-astrid---the-bookish-sweet-tooth">Astrid - The Bookish Sweet Tooth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2006997794" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18163345320209179242">✬✬✬ 5 "I'M NOBODY" STARS ✬✬✬<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495956896i/22870288._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a href='http://coffeecookieandbooks.blogspot.com/2017/05/5-im-nobody-stars-amy-harmon-different.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review @ Vanilla & Spice Books</a><br/><br/><br/>The book market is so saturated that it's impossible to read every author, especially with the limited time I have. So please forgive me that this is my first Amy Harmon book. It definitely won't be my last.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“I’m nobody!<br/> Who are you?<br/> Are you nobody, too?<br/> Then there’s a pair of us— don’t tell<br/> They’d banish us, you know."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br/><br/>Blue Echohawk isn't a conformist. She is around 19 years old, she dresses trashy to provoke, is always late a</span>
  <span id="freeText18163345320209179242" style="display:none">✬✬✬ 5 "I'M NOBODY" STARS ✬✬✬<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495956896i/22870288._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="http://coffeecookieandbooks.blogspot.com/2017/05/5-im-nobody-stars-amy-harmon-different.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review @ Vanilla &amp; Spice Books</a><br><br><br>The book market is so saturated that it's impossible to read every author, especially with the limited time I have. So please forgive me that this is my first Amy Harmon book. It definitely won't be my last.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“I’m nobody!<br> Who are you?<br> Are you nobody, too?<br> Then there’s a pair of us— don’t tell<br> They’d banish us, you know."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br><br>Blue Echohawk isn't a conformist. She is around 19 years old, she dresses trashy to provoke, is always late at school and the boys think she's easy and she doesn't have many friends. Blue nourishes that image with her behavior. It's her senior year at high school, all students her age have already graduated. Blue started school later in her life, her story is unusual. She was left behind in the truck of a drifter when she was only two years or so old. He took her under his wing and raised her and taught her how to carve beautiful sculptures. The mystery of her birth has never been solved.<br><br>It's the first day after summer break and Blue is again late for the last class of the day. History, her least favorite subject. And there is a new teacher, a young handsome guy with a British accent and a love for books and history. She dislikes him because he asks uncomfortable questions, questions that are too personal and she'll be damned if she shared her story with a stranger. And who the hell names their kid Darcy Wilson?<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>...as different as Wilson was from all the boys I’d ever known. And it wasn’t just the way he talked. It was him. His light and his intensity. And I hated him for it.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489734970i/22243857._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This story is about Blue, all other characters, including the hero are support acts. Don't get me wrong, I loved Wilson, he is amazing with her but she is the character this story focuses on and she is unforgettable. Blue is portrayed to be defiant and disrespectful. Abrasive even but on this journey she becomes softer, the edges and ripples are smoothed out like the wood she carves. Feeling discarded, unwanted and unworthy Wilson teaches her that her value doesn't lie in her birth but the way she deals with life and her choices.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“There’s no sense in running from the past. We can’t throw it away or pretend it didn’t happen, Miss Echohawk. But maybe we can learn something from it. You have an interesting story, and I’d like you to tell me more.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br><br>Blue faces the tragedy and obstacles with dignity and one experience in particular shows how selfless she is. I cried buckets. I loved this strong heroine, who had to deal with so much sadness in her life, and her journey to become "A Different Blue."<br><br>Wilson is an intriguing mix of wisdom and innocence. He obstinately avoids romantic entanglement with his former student, it's improper regardless of their small difference in age, plus he doesn't know how she feels about him. I loved how he was always there when she needed him. And except for one part of the story towards the end he was easy to love. His inability to get over himself was irritating but understandable at the same time.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“I was afraid, Blue,” he repeated, insistent. “You’ve been through so much. And I am half mad over you. I don’t think you are ready for the way I feel.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br><br>There is a lot of underlying sadness in this story but also an uplifting feeling when it comes to Wilson's and Blue's relationship. I loved their friendship, the way he offered valuable insight and advice and a shoulder if Blue was in need of one.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489734970i/22243857._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Just when I think I know all there is to know, you reveal something that absolutely guts me. I don’t know how you’ve survived, Echohawk. I really don’t. The fact that you’re still making jokes and wishing on streetlights is a bit of a miracle.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br><br>This wonderful and superbly written story is about finding your value and yourself without letting your past rule you. Your identity isn't tied to your origins. The way history and native american legends are woven into this tale is perfectly done and makes for a gripping read. "A Different Blue" is poignant, full of emotion and wisdom. The Pride &amp; Prejudice references tickled my funny bone. Amy Harmon's writing is beautiful and lyrical and I can't wait to read more of her stories!<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“And I love you . . . most ardently,” he responded, twisting my hair in his hands and pulling me toward him.<br> “Pride and Prejudice?”<br> “How did you know?” he smiled.<br> “I have a thing for Mr. Darcy.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <br><br><i>
  <b>"A Different Blue"</b>
</i>is a standalone.<br><br><a href="http://coffeecookieandbooks.blogspot.co.at/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486060125i/21877446._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/VanillaandSpiceBooks/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491980409i/22468566.png" width="50px” height= " class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7420520-astrid" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491980409i/22468570.png" width="50px” height= " class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://twitter.com/VanSpicebooks" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491980409i/22468568.png" width="50px” height= " class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> <a href="https://www.instagram.com/vanillaandspicebooks/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491980409i/22468567.png" width="50px” height= " class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/cordeeh/vanilla-spice-books/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a></span>

<div id="review_1222648584" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1222648584" />
    <a title="Beverly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13095060-beverly"><img alt="Beverly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466964369p2/13095060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1222648584?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beverly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beverly" href="/user/show/13095060-beverly">Beverly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781482658149" href="/book/show/17443673-a-different-blue">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1222648584" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18175619894570842336"><i>A Different Blue</i> is nothing like I expected, I think it’s safe to say that all of Amy’s books are nothing like you would expect. First, it was pitched to me by my bestie as a student/teacher story. Of course I was downloading the audiobook as we spoke…then she says, well it’s really so much more, just read it you will see. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Once upon a time...there was a little blackbird, pushed from the nest. Unwanted. Discarded. </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/>Blue Echohawk is lost. Despite being found and raised by Jimmy, a drift</span>
  <span id="freeText18175619894570842336" style="display:none"><i>A Different Blue</i> is nothing like I expected, I think it’s safe to say that all of Amy’s books are nothing like you would expect. First, it was pitched to me by my bestie as a student/teacher story. Of course I was downloading the audiobook as we spoke…then she says, well it’s really so much more, just read it you will see. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Once upon a time...there was a little blackbird, pushed from the nest. Unwanted. Discarded. </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />Blue Echohawk is lost. Despite being found and raised by Jimmy, a drifter who found her in his truck at a restaurant. She doesn’t know who she is, where she comes from, or even where she truly belongs. She didn’t have a typical upbringing she was abandoned by her mother when she was two and raised by Jimmy. She didn’t attend school until she was ten years old. Now this phase of her life is ending and she has to decide where to go next.<br /><br />Darcy Wilson knows exactly where he is supposed to be, he is older and already gone through a lot of the growing pains of finding himself and learning what he wants. His passion is teaching and he has a very unique way of doing so. So unique that even when his reluctant, stubborn student continues try him at ever turn he doesn’t give up on her. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Life is all we have, and we live it as we believe in living it. But to sacrifice what you are and to live without belief, that is a fate more terrible than dying."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />The friendship between Blue and Wilson is unlikely and unexpected, but just what they both need. If there ever was a case of non-instalove this is it. Like I said this isn’t a student/teacher book, Wilson is more interested in helping and supporting Blue than finding a love connection. He is completely selfless and just wants what’s best for Blue. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I keep wishing you had a better life... a different life. But a different life would have made you a different Blue. And that would be the biggest tragedy of all.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />The story spans over Blue’s senior year and after graduation. I absolutely loved everything about this story. I love the characters. Blue is resilient, determined and real. I feel like Blue is like most girls her age: struggling with who she is, where to go and what to do with her life. I could feel Blue’s emotions and my heart broke for her. I am not sure I have ever been more of a cheerleader for a character in a book. <br /><br />There were multiple times throughout the story I would tear up thinking about Blue and her past. While she comes off as hard and unaffected in the beginning, she is just a girl who wants to be loved and belong. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"There's no sense in running from the past. We can't throw it away or pretend it didn't happen, Miss Echohawk. But maybe we can learn something from it."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />I loved Wilson. He was a great man, unique, charismatic, giving and loving. He was exactly what Blue needs in her life. I love that he saw the real Blue and didn’t want to change anything about her. He just wanted her to find peace in her life, to live her life and not cut herself short. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Girls like me notice guys like you. We just don’t think we deserve them.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />I highly recommend this story! It’s so well written and moving. So while I jumped to purchase this one to feed my forbidden love addiction, I am so glad it turned out to be so much more!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18175619894570842336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_577439129" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/577439129" />
    <a title="Jenny - TotallybookedBlog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3870376-jenny---totallybookedblog"><img alt="Jenny - TotallybookedBlog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554795448p2/3870376.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/577439129?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny - TotallybookedBlog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny - TotallybookedBlog" href="/user/show/3870376-jenny---totallybookedblog">Jenny - TotallybookedBlog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781482658149" href="/book/show/17443673-a-different-blue">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer577439129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1660661198536743081"><b>*******YOU CAN CHECK OUT THE WILSON POV AND INTERVIEW WITH AMY HARMON****** - <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://totallybookedblog.com/2013/04/12/interview-with-amy-harmon-author-of-a-different-blue-and-exclusive-wilson-pov-chapter-one-bold-plus-giveaway/'>http://totallybookedblog.com/2013/04/...</a><br/><br/>*****PLUS!!! CHECK OUT THE EPILOGUE FOR A DIFFERENT BLUE - PLEASE NOTE THIS EPILOGUE CONTAINS SPOILERS IF YOU HAVEN'T READ A DIFFERENT BLUE**** <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://totallybookedblog.com/2013/04/12/exclusive-epilogue-from-a-different-blue-by-amy-harmon/'>http://totallybookedblog.com/2013/04/...</a> <br/></b><br/><br/>4.5 Stars<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Once upon a time…there was a little blackbird, pushed from the next. Unwanted. Discarded”</i>
</b><br/><br/>And so begins A Different Blue. Part of the synopsis sums up the story with <i>“This is the story</i></span>
  <span id="freeText1660661198536743081" style="display:none"><b>*******YOU CAN CHECK OUT THE WILSON POV AND INTERVIEW WITH AMY HARMON****** - <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://totallybookedblog.com/2013/04/12/interview-with-amy-harmon-author-of-a-different-blue-and-exclusive-wilson-pov-chapter-one-bold-plus-giveaway/">http://totallybookedblog.com/2013/04/...</a><br /><br />*****PLUS!!! CHECK OUT THE EPILOGUE FOR A DIFFERENT BLUE - PLEASE NOTE THIS EPILOGUE CONTAINS SPOILERS IF YOU HAVEN'T READ A DIFFERENT BLUE**** <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://totallybookedblog.com/2013/04/12/exclusive-epilogue-from-a-different-blue-by-amy-harmon/">http://totallybookedblog.com/2013/04/...</a> <br /></b><br /><br />4.5 Stars<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Once upon a time…there was a little blackbird, pushed from the next. Unwanted. Discarded”</i>
</b><br /><br />And so begins A Different Blue. Part of the synopsis sums up the story with <i>“This is the story of a nobody who becomes a somebody. It is the story of an unlikely friendship where hope fosters healing and redemption becomes love.”</i><br /><br />Whilst that is a perfect way to summarize this book, it doesn’t even scratch the surface of the content of this story. <br />This book….I really don’t know what to begin to talk about this book. Even as I’m writing this review I am thinking back to the story of Blue and I am welling up. There were times this book lifted my spirits, there were times I felt such inexplicable sorrow for Blue and there were times my heart warmed at the beautiful old soul Wilson and the interaction between him and Blue. What a beautiful combination they were. .<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Don’t let anybody tell you different. Regret is just life’s aftertaste.”</i>
</b><br /><br />This story was beautiful and moving. As heart-warming as it was heartbreaking. As breath-taking as it was overwhelming. I continually stopped to wipe away tears as Blue Echohawk and her story completely and utterly stole my heart. It is a bit difficult to do a review of this book because you can’t divulge too much without giving away spoilers and to do that would be a travesty to this story. It must be experienced and revealed at its own pace, the way the author intended. I want readers to experience this the way I did.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“To live without belief is a fate worse than death”</i>
</b><br /><br />To say Blue has lived a tough life really is an understatement. But she is a survivor.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“It wasn’t much. But I was never hungry, I was never cold, and I don’t remember ever being really unhappy” ….”…..I didn’t know any different so I wasn’t especially lonely”</i>
</b> Blue<br /><br />This girl doesn’t know her real name or when she was born. She was abandoned at two and raised by a drifter, not attending school until she was ten. Blue feels she has no faith and no hope and her attitude at school reflects her feelings. Her dress sense and overall appearance oozes sex appeal as she confuses sex with nurturing as a way of dealing with pain and loneliness.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“God? If you love me…take it away. Please. I’m asking you to take it away. I don’t want to feel this anymore”</i>
</b> Blue<br /><br />I adored Blue. I found her sassy, stoic, with so much heart. Yes she did radiate an attitude from every pore, but it was understandably so. With little or no self esteem or self love, Blue is convinced she is nothing. But you know the girl inside; you feel the girl beyond the attitude is special. You know Blue is a survivor but you will feel every single minute of her struggles. Blue may have not have felt hope but I can assure you I did. I believed in her without exception.<br /><br />When Blue strikes up an unlikely friendship with her new History teacher Mr Wilson in her senior year, theirs is a friendship that is so very special it will completely move you, render you speechless and these two will completely captivate you, I know they did me.<br />What can one say about this Wilson?<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“You can’t control who loves you….you can’t let someone love you anymore than you can make someone love you” </i>
</b><br /><br />There is so much to this man. This guy really is a book hero in every sense of the word. He’s not your alpha type hero, and he doesn’t need to be. He is unique and beautiful inside and out. I completely fell in love with this cheeky, intelligent, funny and sometimes stuffy Brit teacher.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“A handkerchief! What are you eighty five?” </i>
</b> Blue<br /><br />His humor, his soulfulness and his compassion won me over….yes, Wilson was very much the core of this story right along with Blue.<br /><br />Blue’s story unfolds by way of a history assignment in Mr Wilson’s class. Little by little he coaxes her to write about her life.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Don’t worry about being perfect. Perfect is boring” “I just want an honest account – whatever you are willing to divulge”</i>
</b> Wilson<br /><br />Blue is closed, she doesn’t want to let others in and she especially doesn’t want to expose her life in a classroom environment. Watching this friendship develop, watching Blue open up, watching Wilson nurture her….well, as I said, I’m welling up just thinking about it. This book completely moved me.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Some moments you don’t get back, Blue. You don’t want to spend a lifetime wondering about those moments you didn’t seize, about the things you should have done but were too scared to”</i>
</b> Wilson<br /><br />The relationship between Wilson and Blue is the absolutely heart of this story. There’s was a slow build relationship that never felt rushed, never felt contrived.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“We studied each other silently. And then he brought his hand up and laid it gently against my cheek. Such a simple gesture. But it was my undoing. I closed my eyes and cried”</i>
</b> Blue<br /><br />This book is one I won’t forget in a hurry. So, why not a 5 star? Well, for me there were a couple of scenes I would have liked expanded upon, I would have liked some answers to and I really would have loved an epilogue but this in no way detracted from my enjoyment of this story as you can tell.<br /><br />This is so, so much more than a romance story. There is so much to this book that you will at times gasp at what comes next – I know parts completely took me surprise. This book had depth, heart, sorrow, pain, humor, hope and some of the most wonderful, heart stealing characters you could meet, every last one of them. I loved it!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“I keep wishing you had a better life………A different life. But a different life would have made you a different Blue.”</i>
</b> Wilson<br /><br />I’ll leave by saying…...<b>
  <i> “British butts drive me nuts”</i>
</b> haha</span>
  <a data-text-id="1660661198536743081" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_575975836" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/575975836" />
    <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday"><img alt="Ash Wednesday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379043440p2/10484016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/575975836?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash Wednesday" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday">Ash Wednesday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781482658149" href="/book/show/17443673-a-different-blue">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans who want a lecture on British slang, random history , fables and parables</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=i-m-gonna-be-in-the-minority">i-m-gonna-be-in-the-minority</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=review">review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=student-teacher">student-teacher</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer575975836" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13299504971441782768"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415557i/820306.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Felt like having that question on repeat throughout this read.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>2.5 STARS</i>
</b> <br/><br/>Yep, that's me in the corner, me in the spotlight losing a good number of marbles reading this because I'm seriously questioning if I'm an emotional block of concrete or I'm just stars-selfish towards NA books or it really just didn't cut it.<br/><br/>Honestly, I read this book with some wary hostility because for me, <i>
  <b>Slammed</b>
</i> is untouchable and getting this compared to such a beloved book, well big shoes to fill if books have </span>
  <span id="freeText13299504971441782768" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415557i/820306.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Felt like having that question on repeat throughout this read.<br><br><b>
  <i>2.5 STARS</i>
</b> <br><br>Yep, that's me in the corner, me in the spotlight losing a good number of marbles reading this because I'm seriously questioning if I'm an emotional block of concrete or I'm just stars-selfish towards NA books or it really just didn't cut it.<br><br>Honestly, I read this book with some wary hostility because for me, <i>
  <b>Slammed</b>
</i> is untouchable and getting this compared to such a beloved book, well big shoes to fill if books have feet. <i>
  <b> Sea of Tranquility</b>
</i> has also been mentioned in the same manner but I'm not a big fan of that one which is probably <s>not</s> a good gauge of my taste in New Adult books.<br><br>It's safe to say that Will and Lake and that damn purple hair clip rests easy in my pedestal of feels.<br><br>My biggest issue with this book are the main characters: I wasn't charmed, felt no sympathy towards them whatsoever. And the things others may have liked about them are like nails grating on my emotional blackboard.<br><br>The heroine, Blue Echohawk was abandoned by a druggie mother who, before getting killed at the beginning of the story, left her with a stranger whom Blue believed to be her father until he too died. Lots of teen angst right there, which of course is directly proportional to the amount of eye make-up and tight jeans one wears at school. So our Blue is a skank (her words not mine), but she doesn't want to be one. It's just that she doesn't know who she is and where she's heading but this is the only way she could deal.<br><br>Which brings much vacillating between self-loathing and self-pity in pretty much the entire first 50% of the book. This would've been perfectly acceptable to me except, I couldn't join her in the vacillating sessions because she sounds pretty normal and dramatic. In high school. Yeah, shocker. Sure she throws the occasionally flat sass, likes to girly-smirk and does the nasty with a guy (just one guy, mind you) but her behavior didn't feel out of the ordinary.<br><br>Between her and Wilson (I'm sorry but Tom Hanks has ruined this name beyond repair), I think he takes the chunk of the grief I have over this book. His name is Darcy Wilson. He's Blue's British history teacher who lives in a house where he hung a plate in front calling it "Pemberley". And, I kid you not, he dished the "most ardently" line which just, I don't know, makes me squirm with discomfort that leads to full-fledged frowning when he signed himself off as the worst fictional history teacher. EVER.<br><br><i>
  <b>"Literature tells the history so much better than the text books."<br><br>"Never judge history by the so-called facts."</b>
</i><br><br>I feel silly bringing this up but we all know that history should be based on on titanium-strength facts, right? It may not be as romantic as when literature takes its great liberties but taking these liberties as biblical is what gets people burned at pseudo-intellectual coffeehouse conversations. I can't understand why he couldn't have just been the literature teacher since he's so keen on having the students write essays on their personal histories (which is by the way, borderline creepy for a history teacher to ask). Because if this is his effort to deliver his subject matter in a fresh and cool manner, he needs to sit in on the history classes from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244.Unearthly__Unearthly___1_" title="Unearthly (Unearthly, #1) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Unearthly</a>.<br><br>I'm sure there's a subset of women out there who will find Wilson swoon-worthy but I'm afraid the poetry quoting and the cello playing doesn't do it for me. Nor the Peace Corps to Africa gig, especially if you announce it during your lectures. Nice to meet you too, Frodo Douchebaggins.<br><br>There's a lack of finesse and subtlety in the writing and the drama went over the top at certain points (the crying and praying in the hallway with the healing powers of music, ugh) as if beating me up to make me cry ("Cry, b*tch. Cry!") There was some feeble effort for some comic relief but the constant hammering of Britishisms and slangs ceases its novelty and quirk when told in tireless increments. Manny and Gabriela just stopped existing like a pair of Jarjar Binkses and Joss Whedon wasn't even credited for his brilliance***:<br><br><i>
  <b>"Being yourself only works if you don't suck. If you do suck, definitely don't be yourself."</b>
</i><br><br>It did improve by the second half of the book but not by much. Probably because all that silliness about Wilson playing teacher was put to rest and mostly because Tiffa throws awesome New Years parties. I also appreciated the lack of any insta-love between the protagonists but the seeds have already taken root by then and the messy, convoluted resolution didn't do the story any favors. I'm actually having a hard time thinking of what I did like about it. The story felt winded and unnecessarily slow and I just felt tired and thankful when I finally finished this. <br><br>I do feel my gripes are brought on by my personal quirks and pet peeves and I can still see how this can work for others and not for some... or in this case, one.<br><br>***<i>Actual Joss Whedon quote reads: “Remember to always be yourself. Unless you suck.” </i>***</span>
  <a data-text-id="13299504971441782768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=unpopular-opinions">unpopular-opinions</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2028098675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14044214151687089078"><b>2 Stars<br/><br/>Overview: </b><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“Why don’t you focus on where you’re going and less on where you came from?” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>Rating this so low feels weird, because I <i>adored</i> the last Harmon book I read! : <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1898347474' rel='nofollow noopener'>Making Faces</a> broke my heart and made me cry ugly tears. This just wasn’t on the same level. Dry characters made for a boring, flat story. <br/><br/>I received a free copy of this through Netgalley in exchange for an honest review. Thanks to CreateSpace for the opportunity!<br/><br/><b>Pros:</b><br/><br/>Even though I never connected with the characters, thi</span>
  <span id="freeText14044214151687089078" style="display:none"><b>2 Stars<br /><br />Overview: </b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Why don’t you focus on where you’re going and less on where you came from?” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Rating this so low feels weird, because I <i>adored</i> the last Harmon book I read! : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1898347474" rel="nofollow noopener">Making Faces</a> broke my heart and made me cry ugly tears. This just wasn’t on the same level. Dry characters made for a boring, flat story. <br /><br />I received a free copy of this through Netgalley in exchange for an honest review. Thanks to CreateSpace for the opportunity!<br /><br /><b>Pros:</b><br /><br />Even though I never connected with the characters, this plot is powerful. I honestly wasn’t certain the directions this was going to take, and there was a surprising number of twists. <br /><br />There’s a really strong emphasis on the diversity of motherhood, and how there isn’t <i>one</i> good way to be a mom. <br /><br /><b>Cons:</b><br /><br />Why does every British protagonist (written by Americans) constantly remind us <i>they are British??</i> It’s all so posh it’s ridiculous and I’m so tired of the cliche “oh you American’s have silly words for everything.”<br /><br />A lot of this just seemed random? The entire first 25% features completely different characters and plots, without resolution for any of them. I really was intrigued by Manny’s story, but overall, he didn’t add anything to the story? There’s one scene where a main characters has a super spiritual experience that supposedly changes them, but ultimately amounts to nothing? <br /><br />None of the character's worked for me? Blue’s main personality trait seemed to be her abandonment. <i>Everything</i> she did was talk about it, be defensive or struggle with feeling lonely. These are all valid, interesting emotions, but shouldn’t <i>define</i> her. The love interest’s main trait seemed to be that he <i>wasn’t</i> a douchebag (and don’t forget, British!)<br /><br /><b>In Conclusion:</b><br /><br />Maybe it’s me. Maybe I hate love. Maybe I’m just dead inside. <br /></span>

<div id="review_581905520" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/581905520" />
    <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog"><img alt="Aestas Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353371225p2/5604583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/581905520?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aestas Book Blog" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog">Aestas Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781482658149" href="/book/show/17443673-a-different-blue">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer581905520" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2614932968476801595"><img width='100%' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380416406i/822310._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i> <b> <blockquote> “Once upon a time<br/>there was a little blackbird,<br/>pushed from the nest.<br/>Unwanted.<br/>Discarded.” </blockquote> </b></i> <br/><b> This is the story about a lost girl finding herself. And the guy who took her under his wing. </b><br/><br/>This book takes the whole concept of ‘finding yourself’ to a whole new level. Abandoned by her mother at the age of 2, Blue doesn’t know her real name, doesn’t remember her parents, and doesn’t even know when she was born. She came with no immunization records, no address, no birth certificate, nothing. Raised </span>
  <span id="freeText2614932968476801595" style="display:none"><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380416406i/822310._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i> <b> <blockquote> “Once upon a time<br>there was a little blackbird,<br>pushed from the nest.<br>Unwanted.<br>Discarded.” </blockquote> </b></i> <br><b> This is the story about a lost girl finding herself. And the guy who took her under his wing. </b><br><br>This book takes the whole concept of ‘finding yourself’ to a whole new level. Abandoned by her mother at the age of 2, Blue doesn’t know her real name, doesn’t remember her parents, and doesn’t even know when she was born. She came with no immunization records, no address, no birth certificate, nothing. Raised by a drifter, she didn’t even start school until she was 10 making her older than everyone else too. Everything about her life was build on guesses leaving her with no sense of belonging, no belief in anything and in a constant state of trying to make sense of the unknown.<br><br>But her young, new teacher at school takes a special interest in her – curious about what could be behind her story. And through the lessons in his classes, he tries to help her find herself.<br><br>This book is built subtly in many layers. It’s very much a read-between-the-lines kind of book. The history lessons in school and folk lore stories all have parallels that reflect back into Blue’s life.<br><br><blockquote> <i> “What we believe affects our lives in a very real way. What we believe affects our choices, our actions, and subsequently, our lives.” </i>
</blockquote> <br>I’ll admit that the beginning of this story, despite being interesting, was a little slow for me. I struggled with it a little in places but was still intrigued by the story and after about 25% I was sucked in and read the rest of it in one fell swoop.<br><br>I have to say that this book did not go where I was expecting it to – which was something I really liked about it. Each time I thought I had a hold on it’s direction, it switched. Quietly. But completely.<br><br>The primary focus of this story was Blue’s journey of self discovery. Along that journey, she falls in love. But the story’s focus is her, not specifically the romance. That being said, I did find Wilson rather charming in a British school-teacher kind of way. And I loved how he took her under his wing and was always there for her. He didn’t always know what she needed, but he sure tried his best to give it to her.<br><br>Their relationship was very interesting because it was constantly changing. There was no insta-love and no relationship in fact really until well into the second half of the book. Rather, at first their relationship was honestly built more on a mixture of curiosity and caring.<br><br><blockquote> <i> <b>“I keep wishing you had a better life… a different life. But a different life would have made you a different Blue… And that would be the biggest tragedy of all.” </b></i>
</blockquote>  <br><br>This book had no steam, so just don’t go into it expecting that. However there are some very sweet kisses scattered throughout the last half.<br><br>Now, I know a lot of people have said that this book made them cry (ugly tears even) and hit them very strongly emotionally but, despite liking the story, I didn’t actually ever even tear up. It didn’t mean that wasn’t into it, just that, I guess it didn’t affect me that way. Or… maybe my tears are broken? :/<br><br>It’s not a long read, definitely something that can be read in one sitting. I did find myself wishing for a little more detail in certain places and perhaps also for an epilogue but I enjoyed my read and appreciated that, after all the questions the story dug up, that it had a happy, resolved ending.<br><br>The R-words sum up this story perfectly:<br><br><blockquote> <i> <b> Redemption, Resolution, Revelation. </b></i>
</blockquote>  <br><br>CASTING for Wilson (I liked the Blue on the cover)<br><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380416406i/822311._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380416406i/822312.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img width="100%" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1364846607l/17443673.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> For more of my reviews, visit <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Aestas Book Blog</a><br>And come join the Aestas Book Blog <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Aestas-Book-Blog/332404836826905" rel="nofollow noopener"> Facebook Page</a> </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2614932968476801595" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
