<div id="review_2575669619" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2575669619" />
    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2575669619?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17830192-a-different-blue">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2575669619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5289018049022225082">This was such a stunning story. I’m becoming obsessed with Amy Harmon. Her characters and stories are wonderfully rich and engaging, the writing is simple by absolutely full of emotion and tenderness that slowly trickles into your heart and themes that she explores that’ll teach you something about life.<br/><br/><i>‘A Different Blue’</i> was all of those things and more. I couldn’t get enough of the story telling. A story about a girl who’s been abandoned by her mother. <br/>A story about a teacher who loves history</span>
  <span id="freeText5289018049022225082" style="display:none">This was such a stunning story. I’m becoming obsessed with Amy Harmon. Her characters and stories are wonderfully rich and engaging, the writing is simple by absolutely full of emotion and tenderness that slowly trickles into your heart and themes that she explores that’ll teach you something about life.<br /><br /><i>‘A Different Blue’</i> was all of those things and more. I couldn’t get enough of the story telling. A story about a girl who’s been abandoned by her mother. <br />A story about a teacher who loves history told in the form of a story, who takes his students on a journey of growth and self-discovery by letting them draw parallels from history into their lives. <br />It’s a story about art, passion, parenthood and wood carvings. <br /><br />The author really takes the reader on a journey with their characters and I enjoyed slowly uncovering everything. It took me by surprise how much the story hit me. I would put it down and constantly think about the characters and their lives whilst I was occupied doing mundane tasks around the house. <br /><br />The ending was slightly too abrupt for me liking. I would’ve liked for that to have been more drawn out, since revelations came into play. Or an epilogue, at least. Bar that, I thoroughly enjoyed the story and I’m making my way through Amy Harmon’s books now. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5289018049022225082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2952104863" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2952104863" />
    <a title="Starr (AKA Bam Bam) Rivers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74622641-starr-aka-bam-bam-rivers"><img alt="Starr (AKA Bam Bam) Rivers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581473939p2/74622641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

  <span id="freeText2879368143484966831" style="display:none"><b>July 2017 Re-Read!!!</b><br>I just love this book ♥<br><br><b>June 2015 Re-Read!!!</b><br>Sigh...I just adore this book. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17443673.A_Different_Blue" title="A Different Blue by Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">A Different Blue</a> was my first ever <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5829056.Amy_Harmon" title="Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy Harmon</a> novel, it inspired me to make an "absolute favorites" shelf on my goodreads profile (yes <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17443673.A_Different_Blue" title="A Different Blue by Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">A Different Blue</a> was my first favorite book!), and it led me to Ms. Harmon's other amazing work. This story is emotional, humorous, cultural, artistic, spiritual, and beautifully character-driven. This was my second time reading it and my emotions were still on high alert. I was profoundly moved by these characters and their shared journey. Thank you for this experience Ms. Harmon!<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17443673.A_Different_Blue" title="A Different Blue by Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">A Different Blue</a> was recommended to me as a BOTM in one of my favorite goodreads groups. Now, two years later, I have the opportunity to choose a BOTM for a different group and what did I choose? <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17443673.A_Different_Blue" title="A Different Blue by Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">A Different Blue</a> of course! <br><br>If you have never read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5829056.Amy_Harmon" title="Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy Harmon</a> before, I strongly encourage you to. Her list of books is growing and I get so excited every time I hear of a new release. Check her out!<br><br><b>My favorite quote:</b><br><i>“What we believe affects our choices, our actions, and subsequently, our lives. The Greeks believed in their gods, and this belief affected everything else. History is written according to what men believe, whether or not it's true. As the writer of your own history, what you believe influences the paths you take. Do you believe in something that may be a myth? I'm not talking about religious beliefs, per se. I'm talking about things you've told yourself, or things you've been told for so long that you just assume that they are true.”</i><br><br>The following books have been authored by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5829056.Amy_Harmon" title="Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy Harmon</a> as of June 2015. </a><br><br><b>Original Review: June 9, 2013</b><br>I adored this book. Blue's emotions in this story were palpable and brought me to tears at times, and her personal growth was beautful to read. And might I note, everyone should have a teacher, mentor, friend, etc. like Wilson who reminds us that while we all have our personal histories that shape us, ultimately we have control of how our story will end. <br><br>For a long time I've limited myself to fantasy-type genres that let me escape reality for a while. While these genres still remain my favorite, reading A Different Blue has me rethinking why I don't branch out a little. Now that I know there are beautiful gems like this out there I just might. Thank you Amy Harmon!<br><br><b>My favorite quote:</b><br><i>“Sometimes the things we want to be rescued from can save us.”</i></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_576063576" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/576063576" />
    <a title="Michelle [Helen Geek]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5557851-michelle-helen-geek"><img alt="Michelle [Helen Geek]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448463806p2/5557851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/576063576?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle [Helen Geek]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle [Helen Geek]" href="/user/show/5557851-michelle-helen-geek">Michelle [Helen Geek]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781482658149" href="/book/show/17443673-a-different-blue">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who loved Colleen Hoover's Slammed -- this is BETTER!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5557851-michelle-helen-geek?shelf=5_star">5_star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5557851-michelle-helen-geek?shelf=tm_challenge_2013_in_2013">tm_challenge_2013_in_2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5557851-michelle-helen-geek?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5557851-michelle-helen-geek?shelf=tbr-kindle">tbr-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5557851-michelle-helen-geek?shelf=author_love">author_love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5557851-michelle-helen-geek?shelf=ntm_author_2013">ntm_author_2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5557851-michelle-helen-geek?shelf=were-pub-d-in-2013-i-read">were-pub-d-in-2013-i-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5557851-michelle-helen-geek?shelf=life-changing">life-changing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer576063576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7717866683103933821">04/23/2013 – <br/><b><br/>Overall Rating = 5 Stars<br/>Book Cover / Book Blurb = 4 / 4 = 4 Stars<br/>Writer’s Voice = 5 Stars<br/>Character Development = 5 Stars<br/>Story Appreciation = 5 Stars<br/>Worth the Chili = 5 Stars [$3.99 on Amazon]<br/></b><br/>This book would never have made it on my radar if not for this website. I would have missed reading this lovely story, would have missed knowing about this author. For me, this would have been an absolute shame. This is a lovely book. It is the story of one girls struggle to figure it all out. H</span>
  <span id="freeText7717866683103933821" style="display:none">04/23/2013 – <br /><b><br />Overall Rating = 5 Stars<br />Book Cover / Book Blurb = 4 / 4 = 4 Stars<br />Writer’s Voice = 5 Stars<br />Character Development = 5 Stars<br />Story Appreciation = 5 Stars<br />Worth the Chili = 5 Stars [$3.99 on Amazon]<br /></b><br />This book would never have made it on my radar if not for this website. I would have missed reading this lovely story, would have missed knowing about this author. For me, this would have been an absolute shame. This is a lovely book. It is the story of one girls struggle to figure it all out. Her road down a troubled path and then the journey towards Redemption. Sounds really deep, but it is told in such a way that it just pulls you.<br /><br /><b>There wasn’t a single thing I didn’t NOT like about this book, so let me tell you about a few things I LOVED in this story:</b><br />1 – Blue Echohawk. Don’t you just love this name? I live in Native America and I can appreciate this handle. We’ve all read those books about kids who have a difficult time of it. So, what makes this one different? Blue. She is that girl who wants to get “bad” attention. She wears too much makeup and tight revealing clothes with the sneer on her face. She is that girl. She’s the one on the train or the bus stop you don’t want to catch her eye. Beneath it all she really is just a little girl wanting to be loved. Wanting someone to care. What she doesn’t realize is that they do. She has many people in her corner but she is too busy pushing them away to figure it all out. Until she meets someone who isn’t responsive to her pushing back. Who challenges her at her core.<br /><br />2 – This author is brilliant. Her voice throughout this story is so intimate. She grabs you immediately and never lets you go. She takes her story and meanders through developing the characters, building the backstory, she then brings you back to the beginning and you want more, more, more… <br /><br />3 – The message of Redemption. I don’t read Christian books. Never have. I find no enjoyment in the average story of trials, tribulations and redemption through Grace. You have to look really hard, but this author gives it to you. It is very, very subtle, but it is there. This tells me this author has believes at her very core. It isn’t something she shouts in the streets about, but it is a part of her DNA. You will almost miss it is so subtle. I hope me mentioning this won’t keep you from reading this book. It shouldn’t. Not at all.<br /><br />4 – The use of art in various forms of media. Blue saved herself, but she had help along the way. At every step art was there. Whether it was Jimmy reaching out to her in the only way he knew how to; through his wood carving. Wilson through his magnificent cello playing or his application of poetry like Dickenson or Poe. At many places in this tale the author reaches you and pulls you along with history, literature and an art form you appreciate, you visualize. You can tell she knows this or has performed sufficient research to paint this believable picture for you.<br /><br />5 – There wasn’t a single character in this book you didn’t get to know intimately. You may have only caught a glimpse of them, but you know them. She told you through words, a richly painted backdrop or through words left unspoken about these characters. You loved them or not, but you definitely appreciated them. They helped Blue come full circle. Mason, for me, was probably the most interesting. He was a guy like any guy at 21 or so. He was all caught up in himself, with little planning of a future. It was just going to happen a day at a time. Until SMACK, life hit him dead center. He rose above himself and did the absolute right thing and you just wanted to cry. He was only in this story for a short time, but you know in your heart of hearts he will regret this decision for the rest of his life. You just know it. He knew it. In the end, he knew it was right for the person that mattered. This author gave this to you.<br /><br />I could go on and on and on. I’ve probably already bored you to tears. The funny thing? GoodReads crapped out on me and this review twice already. I’ve written this darned thing three times now. Why? I want you to read this book. If something I’ve said make you think twice about it or maybe buy it and put it on the top of your pile or maybe you start reading it THIS VERY MOMENT, then my time has been well spent. You owe it to you to read this book. It is a joy.<br /><br />Happy Reading!<br /><br /><i>Note: If you liked Colleen Hoover’s SLAMMED, you’ll love this because it is BETTER THAN!<br /></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7717866683103933821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1982201355" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1982201355" />
    <a title="Christie«SHBBblogger»" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6650940-christie-shbbblogger"><img alt="Christie«SHBBblogger»" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537729030p2/6650940.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1982201355?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christie«SHBBblogger»" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christie«SHBBblogger»" href="/user/show/6650940-christie-shbbblogger">Christie«SHBBblogger»</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6650940-christie-shbbblogger?shelf=why-didnt-i-read-this-earlier">why-didnt-i-read-this-earlier</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1982201355" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6435693637009656582"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396539003i/9148958.jpg' width='400' height='40' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430781898i/14762044.png' width='100' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>Title:</b> A Different Blue<br/><b>Series:</b> Standalone<br/><b>Author:</b> Amy Harmon<br/><b>Release date: </b> May 29, 2017 (Publisher re-release)<br/><b>Cliffhanger:</b> No<br/><b>HEA</b><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Yes <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/>Can you imagine how lost you would feel to not know your own story? Where you came from, and who gave birth to you? Even the most basic DNA of our identity: your own true name and age? This was Blue Echohawk's reality. Jimmy Echohawk, the man who raised her, was a odd sort. Quiet and taciturn. He lived a simple life with her, on the road</span>
  <span id="freeText6435693637009656582" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396539003i/9148958.jpg" width="400" height="40" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430781898i/14762044.png" width="100" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Title:</b> A Different Blue<br><b>Series:</b> Standalone<br><b>Author:</b> Amy Harmon<br><b>Release date: </b> May 29, 2017 (Publisher re-release)<br><b>Cliffhanger:</b> No<br><b>HEA</b><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Can you imagine how lost you would feel to not know your own story? Where you came from, and who gave birth to you? Even the most basic DNA of our identity: your own true name and age? This was Blue Echohawk's reality. Jimmy Echohawk, the man who raised her, was a odd sort. Quiet and taciturn. He lived a simple life with her, on the road selling his wood carvings. And for a time, she was carefree and happy. But after he passed away when she was eleven, she went to live with her aunt Cheryl. And life as she knew it was gone. She became a self-destructive girl, void of hope or self respect.<br><br><b>Jimmy’s little blackbird died a slow and painful death. In her place I built a gaudy, colorful, blue bird. A loud, obnoxious peacock with bright feathers, who dressed to call attention to her beauty at every moment, and craved affection. But it was all just a bright disguise.</b><br><br>On the first day of her senior year in high school, she walked into her history class and met Mr. Wilson. He would come to be the first positive influence in her life since she was a little girl. He's only a few years older than her, but has so much knowledge to give. He saw the hardened, angry girl that she was and made it his mission to get her to open up. Their relationship was completely platonic. He started out as her teacher, her guide, someone she could depend on and trust. When she was at her lowest points and most joyful moments, it was Wilson that saw her through it all. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496102745ra/22882134.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Blue and Wilson had a beautiful friendship. It brought tears to my eyes so many times to see how he gently nudged her into believing in herself again. She had been through so much hopelessness it makes you want to wrap your arms around her and make everything better. Her aunt did her best, but didn't give her the time of day. So when someone showed interest in her, treated her as if she had value and worth, she soaked it all up like a sponge. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429506699ra/14597254.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Wilson was an exceptional man. I loved him so, so much. He was extremely wise, funny, giving, and wonderfully endearing in a nerdy sort of way. Growing up in a wealthy British family, he had many more advantages in life than she had. Yet he wasn't snobbish or self-entitled, quite the opposite. And he accepted Blue, scars and all. <br><br><b>“I keep wishing you had had a better life . . . a different life. But a different life would have made you a different Blue.” He looked at me then. “And that would be the biggest tragedy of all.”</b><br><br>Everyone has a story. Even if her beginning was blank, he helped her see that her future was wide open for her to shape. But just when she started to stretch her wings and fly, she suddenly plunged to the ground. Broken again. She had yet another setback, and my heart broke for her all over again. After graduating high school, Wilson offers her an apartment in his home so that she can get back on her feet and pursue her love of art. Blue made stunning sculptures that she carved out of trees and branches. It helped her to feel close to Jimmy and it was an outlet to express herself. <br><br>Resolution.<br>Redemption.<br>Revelations.<br><br>These are the themes of <i>A Different Blue.</i> There was so much to love about this book. I wouldn't even necessarily say that the romance is what you will focus on. It's pretty much secondary to Blue's own personal struggle to rip off the labels that have placed on her. Her triumph over the mystery of her past, and owning her true self. To see her growth from the brittle and sulky girl, to the strong woman who finally found peace really touched my heart. Both characters were far from perfect, and made human mistakes and decisions that we could all probably relate to. That's why I think I really identified with this story and it's uplifting message. I would recommend this book to anyone and everyone looking for something with real depth and substance. <br><br>**This is a publisher re-release with a bonus epilogue and scene from Wilson's POV. I think the epilogue was a perfect conclusion that left me so satisfied. And I was pretty giddy over getting rare glimpse inside Wilson's head. HIGHLY recommend even for a re-read just to get these new additions to the story.<br><br><b>FOLLOW SMOKIN HOT BOOK BLOG ON: <b><br><br><a href="https://twitter.com/BlogSmokin/" target="_blank"     <a title="Snow" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31719636-snow"><img alt="Snow" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465808156p2/31719636.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2104394019?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Snow" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Snow" href="/user/show/31719636-snow">Snow</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17830192-a-different-blue">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2104394019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18077868169894941373">Amy Harmon is "it" for me, I have decided.<br/><br/>Every book of hers, just fulfills me completely, within...<br/><br/>and afterwards <b>I either feel elevated, apprehensive or even sullen</b>...but I always carry a piece of her messages with me...<br/><br/>And this story ain't no different.<br/><br/>A story of the search for fulfillment/completion on a journey of <i>self-discovery, self-appreciation, self-esteem</i> of a young girl/woman <b>Blue Echohawk</b>, who doesn't really know who she is, regarding the actual facts in documentation. She has none. </span>
  <span id="freeText18077868169894941373" style="display:none">Amy Harmon is "it" for me, I have decided.<br /><br />Every book of hers, just fulfills me completely, within...<br /><br />and afterwards <b>I either feel elevated, apprehensive or even sullen</b>...but I always carry a piece of her messages with me...<br /><br />And this story ain't no different.<br /><br />A story of the search for fulfillment/completion on a journey of <i>self-discovery, self-appreciation, self-esteem</i> of a young girl/woman <b>Blue Echohawk</b>, who doesn't really know who she is, regarding the actual facts in documentation. She has none. She was left on a truckstop by her 19 year old mother and she never knew who she was, and when she was found by a Native American , <b>James Echohawk</b> who raised Blue, as his own, the best way he knew...it was the only life she knew...but never thought of being truly hers.<br /><br />Blue is a girl, who is lost inside, still insecure about her worth as a human being, as a person worthy of love...<br /><br />cause if that were the case, why did her mother leave her in the fist place...<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Once upon a time . . . there was a little blackbird,. . . pushed out of the nest, unwanted."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />She relied on her looks alone, she is desperate for <i>attention, love, compassion and comfort</i>...and she searches in all the wrong places...<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Jimmy's little blackbird died a slow and painful death. In her place I built a gaudy, colorful, blue bird. A loud, obnoxious peacock with bright feathers, who dressed to call attention to her beauty at every moment, and craved affection. But it was all just a bright disguise.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />It will take a lot of patience, persuation and affection of one young man, <b>Darcy Wilson</b> to break that feeling of loss...and misguidance...<br /><br />It will take a lot of push and pull for them both to acknowledge themselves and the growing feelings that will eventually free them both as they find the facts, accept the past and realize that they have come together in full circle...<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Once upon a time there was a little bird who was placed in a nest. Wanted. Cherished. Unafraid, because she knew she was a hawk, a beautiful bird, worthy of awe, deserving of love.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />This was a beautifully written story, filled with remarkable re-telling of tribe legends, that were so miraculously interwined with the lives of main characters, and once again i found that very inspiring. <br /><br />P.s. being a movie freak as well as an avid reader, I couldnt help but notice the minor mischief with the facts😒 *shrugs* <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[there are many adaptations of Jane Austen's masterpiece <i>Pride and Prejudice</i> but the ones mentioned here, should be stated clear as they are in fact: <b>Colin Firth</b> played Mr. Darcy in a TV series Pride &amp; prejudice along side <b>Jennifer Ehle</b> as Elisabeth Bennet BUT in a 2005 movie adaptation <b>Keira Knightely</b> played E. Bennet and <b>Matthew MacFayden</b> played Mr. Darcy, even though, in my humble opinion, <b>Colin Firth</b> IS the perfect Mr. Darcy and that will never change <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="18077868169894941373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8191340-lise-friends-don-t-flag?shelf=made-me-feel">made-me-feel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8191340-lise-friends-don-t-flag?shelf=ya-na">ya-na</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8191340-lise-friends-don-t-flag?shelf=teacher-student-love">teacher-student-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8191340-lise-friends-don-t-flag?shelf=2013-faves">2013-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer573582342" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9433334841049198970"> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415223i/819554.png' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <blockquote>
  <b>“Once upon a time there was a little blackbird, pushed from the nest, unwanted. Discarded. Then a Hawk found her and swooped her up and carried her away, giving her a home in his nest, teaching her to fly. But one day the Hawk didn't come home, and the little bird was alone again, unwanted. She wanted to fly away.”</b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380415223ra/819555.gif' width='300' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Everyone has a story. Every thing has a story</i>
</b><br/>Blue Echohawk and her journey of discovering who she is and what her story is was told in such a way that I now have a new favori</span>
  <span id="freeText9433334841049198970" style="display:none"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415223i/819554.png" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <blockquote>
  <b>“Once upon a time there was a little blackbird, pushed from the nest, unwanted. Discarded. Then a Hawk found her and swooped her up and carried her away, giving her a home in his nest, teaching her to fly. But one day the Hawk didn't come home, and the little bird was alone again, unwanted. She wanted to fly away.”</b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380415223ra/819555.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>Everyone has a story. Every thing has a story</i>
</b><br>Blue Echohawk and her journey of discovering who she is and what her story is was told in such a way that I now have a new favorite heroine. The author unfolded Blue’s life using references to Native American lore, literature<br>and history lessons; so well done and so very captivating. <br>Of course the British history teacher, Mr. Wilson was an amazing catalyst in helping Blue find herself, her story. I was mesmerized by Darcy Wilson’s lessons, in and out of the classroom and his humor, compassion, love of music and appreciation of Blue’s artistry made me fall in love with him right along with Blue.<br><br>At times I was frustrated with his unyielding restraint when it came to admitting and showing his love in a physically sense, but the adoration, concern and guidance he provided Blue was unflappable. <br>Darcy had a very interesting life story as well and the realness and depth in which the author wrote these MC’s allowed me to have one of the strongest connections I have felt for book characters. They jumped off of the pages and right into my heart and head.<br><br>The secondary characters were just as amazing and I laughed out loud at the things that came out of Tiffa’s, (Darcy’s sister) mouth: <br><b>
  <i>“I could eat a unicorn and pick my teeth with his horn! I'm absolutely famished.”</i>
</b><br><br>I was also heartbroken over the events that Blue’s buddies, Manny and Graciela, had to endure. <br>And even though Blue’s caregiver, Jimmy was long gone, he was not forgotten and the things he taught Blue truly molded her life into something worth living. <br><br>But life would take a few unexpected turns for Blue and at times I thought she may take the path her Mother had and I was worried until Blue applied the four R’s to her life: <b>Redemption, Resolution, Revelation, and Relevance.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“One life is all we have and we live it as we believe in living it. But to sacrifice what you are and to live without belief, that is a fate more terrible than dying”~ Joan of Arc</b>
</blockquote><br>I highly recommend this book to all readers that are in the mood for an amazing experience. One that is like admiring an incredible piece of art work, and remember:<br><blockquote>
  <b>“That's the beauty of art,” everyone has their own interpretation.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415223i/819556._SY540_.jpg" width="3500" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </span>
  <a data-text-id="9433334841049198970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1289062558" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1289062558" />
    <a title="Kaila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35924884-kaila"><img alt="Kaila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533304308p2/35924884.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1289062558?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaila" href="/user/show/35924884-kaila">Kaila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781482658149" href="/book/show/17443673-a-different-blue">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=stay-with-me-forever">stay-with-me-forever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=swoon-worthy-love-interest">swoon-worthy-love-interest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=slow-burn">slow-burn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=best-heroines">best-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=re-reads">re-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=breathtakingly-beautiful">breathtakingly-beautiful</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1289062558" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7368627859875361475"><b>RE-READ: January 2018</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>“He had become the most relevant thing in my life. Redemption, resolution, revelation, and now relevance.” </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>5/5 stars</b><br/><br/>Yep, this is still one of my <b>all time favourite </b>romance books. I had a really bad day yesterday, and I don't know anything that can make me feel better than re-reading an old favourite, so I did. This book just brought back all the emotions I remember from time first time, making my heart bleed for the characters. This is my first re-read of the novel, but </span>
  <span id="freeText7368627859875361475" style="display:none"><b>RE-READ: January 2018</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“He had become the most relevant thing in my life. Redemption, resolution, revelation, and now relevance.” </b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>5/5 stars</b><br /><br />Yep, this is still one of my <b>all time favourite </b>romance books. I had a really bad day yesterday, and I don't know anything that can make me feel better than re-reading an old favourite, so I did. This book just brought back all the emotions I remember from time first time, making my heart bleed for the characters. This is my first re-read of the novel, but every time I'm feeling down I read small passages, making me feel like I've read this 100 times. I just have such <b>admiration </b>for Amy Harmon and her writing style, especially the way she draws me into a story and makes me emotionally invested immediately. <i>A Different Blue</i> is a slow burn love story about a lost girl and the man that helps her find herself. Plus, that guy just so happens to be English, cheeky and super sweet. Once again, <b>I fell in love </b>with Wilson and Blue's story, <b>feeling all the emotions </b>along the way with them.<br /><br />Blue Echohawk doesn't know who she really is. Her mother left her with a man when she was very young and this man became her father. But when he died, Blue Echohawk was left feeling lost as she didn't even have a name or a birthday that is really her own. So when her new history teacher, Mr. Wilson, tries to make her tell her story, she is at a loss for words. For someone like her, high school is not easy, and she floats around feeling lost in her life. All Blue has is her wood carving to get her through these hard times, which continues even after she leaves high school. During her last year of school and even afterwards, Wilson becomes an unlikely person that Blue turns to for support, friendship and maybe even love.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“Once upon a time…there was a little blackbird, pushed from the nest. Unwanted. Discarded” </b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>This is just a gorgeous romance book</b>. The beauty of the book slowly but surely enveloped me, until I was fully wrapped up in the book. This book has become a staple in my life. It's just such a strong, heartwarming story and I love it completely. Yes, the romance is a major part of the story, but the book also focuses on self love, redemption and identity. The themes of the story tie perfectly with the romance, making this a heart-wrenching but emotionally fulfilling read. It's so hard to read other romance books after this one, because my standards are immediately elevated.<br /><br />I don't know how many times I can say how <b>perfect</b> I found this relationship to be, but I guess I'm doing it again. At first I thought this would be a sort of teacher/student forbidden relationship, but it turned out to be so much more than that. There is no romantic relationship while Blue is still in high school, but rather a friendship develops first. <b>I really loved </b>these scenes in which Blue and Wilson were getting to know each other, because their connection was so intense. Even if it wasn't sexual at first, I got goosebumps reading theses earlier scenes again, because the connection between these characters is unreal. Throughout the book this relationship blossomed into so much more, and ends up being a fully fledged romance. It's definitely a slow burn romance, with a lot of emotional chemistry, sexual tension and ultimately, love.<br /><br />I really enjoy the use of literature in this story, and how it plays a large role in Blue's journey. As a lover of poetry myself, I just really appreciated the portrayal of how strongly the written verse can affect a person. I also loved how the quotes in the book tied in with Blue figuring out who she is and who she wants to be.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“You’re wrong about one thing, though. Girls like me notice guys like you. We just don’t think we deserve them.”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Blue's character development is <b>phenomenal! </b>At the beginning of the book when we meet her, we get the impression that she is a bit of bitch. She is sarcastic, makes fun of her teachers and is very much a hard-ass. But the more we delve into the story, the more we uncover her vulnerabilities and why she is so lost. Her childhood was definitely bizarre and harsh and considering she didn't know who she really was her sense of identity was quite muddled, but this slowly changed throughout the book. A lot of her development happened on her own, but Wilson was constantly there supporting her. She grew into herself so well and began a journey of self love. By the end of the book she was a truly changed character with a real sense of identity. This development was subtly powerful and phemonelaly written. <b>I truly loved it.</b><br /><br />This book definitely focuses on Blue and her development, but I cannot forget to discuss Wilson. He is just such a great hero, who I love completely. He is a bit of a nerd who loves history, literature of music. When Blue used her strength and anger to protect herself from the world, Wilson used his love and openness. He was a supportive, sweet and loveable character, who I appreciated immensely. I also loved the Britishness of his character, as he often used English slang that I found so endearing. I just can't help but smile when I think of his character. He is definitely one of my favourite romance heroes of all time, and I wouldn't mind jumping into this book to steal him.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“Someone told me once that to create true art you must be willing to bleed and let others watch.”</b>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="7368627859875361475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_624580472" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/624580472" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/624580472?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781482658149" href="/book/show/17443673-a-different-blue">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=best-of-the-best">best-of-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=indie">indie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=the-book-boy-is-mine">the-book-boy-is-mine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=standalone-non-speculative-fiction">standalone-non-speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=it-burns-us-precious">it-burns-us-precious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=hawt-for-teacher">hawt-for-teacher</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer624580472" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16289328183645491894">I read a lot. A LOT. I don't mind admitting that most of what I read these days is fluff. As an English major, I had enough required reading to last a lifetime. Fluff makes me happy. That being said, I blow through fluff. Like a maniac. It's not uncommon for me to devour an entire book in one sitting. I start it. I finish it. I like it, or I don't, and not much thought is required in that determination. That's why I don't often write reviews. "Yay" or "Nay" does not a book review make. <br/><br/>HOWEVER, </span>
  <span id="freeText16289328183645491894" style="display:none">I read a lot. A LOT. I don't mind admitting that most of what I read these days is fluff. As an English major, I had enough required reading to last a lifetime. Fluff makes me happy. That being said, I blow through fluff. Like a maniac. It's not uncommon for me to devour an entire book in one sitting. I start it. I finish it. I like it, or I don't, and not much thought is required in that determination. That's why I don't often write reviews. "Yay" or "Nay" does not a book review make. <br /><br />HOWEVER, this book gutted me. I started it last night, finally crashed halfway in, and refused to pick it up today until I got home from my best friend's bridal shower this afternoon b/c I knew that if I started reading it again, I probably wouldn't make the shower. <br /><br />There is so much that makes this story something IMMENSE, that I'm overwhelmed even contemplating how to communicate it all. <br /><br />I think I'll try a list:<br /><br />1. I typically hate student/teacher entanglements. Why? Because they're entanglements. I'm sorry, it's just not something I can get down with. I had a few crushes on teachers, so I get the appeal, but as an adult I'm totally skeeved out by the idea. <br /><br />Blue and Wilson are not an entanglement. This is possible b/c the story takes place over such a long period of time (incidentally this also makes the story more believable). The relationship progresses in such a way that when it finally becomes romantic, it's not inappropriate.<br /><br />2. I won't go so far as to say that the relationship between Blue and Wilson is secondary to Blue's individual journey of self-discovery, but it's close. The relationship is big and consuming, but Blue's personal growth is the main focus. So yeah. Maybe I will say that romance is secondary to personal growth. <br /><br />3. The way the road of Blue's self-discovery is paved will. GUT. You. If you're human. If you've read it, you'll know what I'm referring to. If you haven't, you will when you get there. But the circumstances leading up to Blue sitting in that hallway, listening to Wilson play the cello . . . and when he plays "Amazing Grace" . . . <br /><br /><i>"I didn't know what grace was, but maybe it sounded like the music. Maybe that was what I was feeling. How sweet the sound. And it was sweet, impossibly so. How sweet the sound that saved a wretch like me. Was a wretch the same thing as a bitch? Or a slut?"</i><br /><br />Do you feel that the way that I do? Does it settle like feathers into your soul? Oh Blue . . . <br /><br />A Different Blue is a beautiful story of a lost girl who finds her way. What grows between Blue and Wilson is also beautiful, but the love they share would be impossible if Blue had not found herself first. Separately, the two stories are wonderful. Together . . . words cannot suffice.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16289328183645491894" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2068877311" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2068877311" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2473504-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1394406877p2/2473504.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2068877311?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/2473504-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer2973073501194933790">Yes, I've read this three times already...but I've not been exposed to the bonus content!! For the purposes of this NetGalley review, I will repost my original review for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30027408.A_Different_Blue' title='A Different Blue by Amy Harmon' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Different Blue</a> and will add a section to review the generous bonus additions incorporated in this 2017 edition. <br/><br/><b>Book Review:</b><br/>Sigh...I just adore this book. A Different Blue was my first ever Amy Harmon novel, it inspired me to make an "absolute favorites" shelf on my digital bookshelf (yes A Different Blue was my first favorit</span>
  <span id="freeText2973073501194933790" style="display:none">Yes, I've read this three times already...but I've not been exposed to the bonus content!! For the purposes of this NetGalley review, I will repost my original review for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30027408.A_Different_Blue" title="A Different Blue by Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">A Different Blue</a> and will add a section to review the generous bonus additions incorporated in this 2017 edition. <br /><br /><b>Book Review:</b><br />Sigh...I just adore this book. A Different Blue was my first ever Amy Harmon novel, it inspired me to make an "absolute favorites" shelf on my digital bookshelf (yes A Different Blue was my first favorite book!), and it led me to Ms. Harmon's other amazing work. This story was emotional, humorous, cultural, artistic, spiritual, and beautifully character-driven. Blue's emotions in this story were palpable and brought me to tears at times, and her personal growth was beautiful to read. And might I note, everyone should have a teacher, mentor, friend, etc. like Wilson who reminds us that while we all have our personal histories that shape us, ultimately we have control of how our story will end. No matter how many times I read this, my emotions are still on high alert and I am profoundly moved by these characters and their shared journey. Thank you for this experience Ms. Harmon!<br /><br /><b>Bonus Content:</b><br />#1- EPILOGUE: LOST AND THEN FOUND: A spontaneous makeout session between Blue and Wilson. Nothing too graphic.<br />#2- WILSON'S CHAPTER: Wilson's POV of his first encounter with Blue.<br /><br /><b>Thank you to the following for permitting me access to an advance reader's copy (ARC) of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30027408.A_Different_Blue" title="A Different Blue by Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">A Different Blue</a>. This generosity did not impact my honesty when rating/reviewing.<br />Source:</b> NetGalley<br /><b>Author:</b> Amy Harmon<br /><b>Publisher:</b> Spencer Hill Press<br /><b>Pub Date:</b> 30 May 2017 </span>

<div id="review_747539405" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/747539405" />
    <a title="bibliophile (Romance Addict) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17937691-bibliophile-romance-addict"><img alt="bibliophile (Romance Addict) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427910066p2/17937691.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/747539405?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="bibliophile (Romance Addict) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="bibliophile (Romance Addict) " href="/user/show/17937691-bibliophile-romance-addict">bibliophile (Romance Addict) </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781482658149" href="/book/show/17443673-a-different-blue">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17937691-bibliophile-romance-addict?shelf=teacher-student">teacher-student</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer747539405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8480214639607561212"><br/>A different Blue by Amy Harmon is a sensational novel about growing up, and getting over hardship. It's a tale of a lost soul looking for home, and never finding it. Blue Echohawk is a ninteen years old senior in high school who has a reputation of a slut. Her life has always been miserable, and she dealt with it secretely until a new history teacher arrive to her school, and teach her. <br/> <br/>This is not a story about forbidden love, but a marverlous novel about healing, and about looking for these p</span>
  <span id="freeText8480214639607561212" style="display:none"><br>A different Blue by Amy Harmon is a sensational novel about growing up, and getting over hardship. It's a tale of a lost soul looking for home, and never finding it. Blue Echohawk is a ninteen years old senior in high school who has a reputation of a slut. Her life has always been miserable, and she dealt with it secretely until a new history teacher arrive to her school, and teach her. <br> <br>This is not a story about forbidden love, but a marverlous novel about healing, and about looking for these people who matter. <br> <br><b>“Sometimes the things we want to be rescued from can save us.” </b><br> <br>● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ●<br><br> <a href="http://s1219.photobucket.com/user/meemoo229/media/IMG_0328.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426939816i/14127855._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_0328.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ●<br> <br>Wilson is Blue's new history teacher. He is wise, and different. He's british, and has an accent that the whole school try to mimic. He's also young, which explains Blue's attraction to him. I also love how he's not perfect. He isn't like most hero's where he will sweep the girl off her feet from the first moment he meets her until the end. No, he's different. Yes, he does help her on so many level, but at the same time he's imperfect which makes him even more likable. He cares about Blue, but at the same time, he's like any guy, can make mistakes. <br><br>Blue is one of my most favorite Heroines EVER! She was not a weak girl who was afraid of others judgment, and although she have made so many mistakes throughout the book, I got to like her. She actually became one of my most favorite heroines. She did seem different at first. Very 'slutty', and doesn't care, but by reading, we find out that she didn't do that for lust. I really like her character development, and I was so happy when I read how strong and successful she became. I swear, I was happy as if I was her friend. <br> <br>● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ●<br> <br><b>“I keep wishing you had had a better life...a different life. But a different life would have made you a different Blue." He looked at me then. "And that would be the biggest tragedy of all.” <br> <br>“Someone told me once that to create true art you must be willing to bleed and let others watch.” </b><br> <br>● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ●<br><br><a href="http://s1219.photobucket.com/user/meemoo229/media/IMG_0334.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426939816i/14127856._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo IMG_0334.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ●<br> <br>One of the best elements of this book is its symbolism. I actually started reading this book with no expectations. I was afraid I might find it a bit boring because I have read 'Making Faces' by Amy Harmon, and it wasn't my cup of tea. However, this books gripped me from the prologue. I was so confused, and I wanted to read more. There were so many plot twists that I didn't even see coming. I loved how Blue dealt with these problems even though some solutions were clearly wrong. It just shows how imperfect she is, and it made the flow of the story more realistic. <br> <br>This book is NOT about romance only. It's about so many things, about healing, moving on, seeing the positive in life, and growing up! It's about goals, and freedom. History, and even birds (I love the stories). This was a very amazing book that I have laughed so hard while reading. Cried my eyes out with disbelief, and shocked out of my head with the plot twists I was never expecting. <br> <br>● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ●<br><br><b>
  <i>**This is not the whole review, if you want to read more gushing about this amazing book, click below!!**</i>
</b><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://thebooksloversbff.wix.com/bookslovers#!A-Different-Blue/c1xse/550ab8570cf292acc4b46284">http://thebooksloversbff.wix.com/book...</a><br> </span>

<div id="review_583075125" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/583075125" />
    <a title="&quot;That&#39;s All&quot; Ash" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5606933-that-s-all-ash"><img alt="&quot;That&#39;s All&quot; Ash" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391795207p2/5606933.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/583075125?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="&quot;That&#39;s All&quot; Ash" class="user" itemprop="url" name="&quot;That&#39;s All&quot; Ash" href="/user/show/5606933-that-s-all-ash">&quot;That&#39;s All&quot; Ash</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781482658149" href="/book/show/17443673-a-different-blue">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5606933-that-s-all-ash?shelf=wow">wow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5606933-that-s-all-ash?shelf=amazing">amazing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5606933-that-s-all-ash?shelf=best-heroines">best-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5606933-that-s-all-ash?shelf=i-heart">i-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5606933-that-s-all-ash?shelf=refreshing">refreshing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5606933-that-s-all-ash?shelf=swoonworthy-characters">swoonworthy-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5606933-that-s-all-ash?shelf=lessons-learned">lessons-learned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer583075125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3981230311795557844"><b>
  <i> Once upon a time there was a little blackbird, pushed from the nest, unwanted. Discarded. Then a Hawk found her and swooped her up and carried her away, giving her a home in his nest, teaching her to fly. But one day the Hawk didn’t come home, and the little bird was alone again, unwanted. She wanted to fly away. But as she rose to the edge of the nest and looked out across the sky, she noticed how small her wings were, how weak. She was trapped. She could fly away, but where would she go? </i>
</b></span>
  <span id="freeText3981230311795557844" style="display:none"><b>
  <i> Once upon a time there was a little blackbird, pushed from the nest, unwanted. Discarded. Then a Hawk found her and swooped her up and carried her away, giving her a home in his nest, teaching her to fly. But one day the Hawk didn’t come home, and the little bird was alone again, unwanted. She wanted to fly away. But as she rose to the edge of the nest and looked out across the sky, she noticed how small her wings were, how weak. She was trapped. She could fly away, but where would she go? </i>
</b><br><br>Blue Echohawk. It’s the kind of name that’s an identity in itself, isn’t it?<br><br>But a name isn’t everything. Especially for Blue. <br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/tumblr_lw94smGjxc1qmmscjo1_500.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <span>[image error]</span>
</a><br><br>She’s just a girl with no one and nothing on the back roads to nowhere. An empty tip jar of a girl who keeps giving herself away like loose change. Her mind is suitcase filled with thread-bare sins. And she’s beautiful to the point where it doesn’t even matter.<br><br>Until she meets the one person who makes her decide to take the shavings of her discarded past and carve a redeeming future for herself.<br><br><b>
  <i> I slid down against the wall until I was sitting on the cool linoleum floor. I leaned my heavy head against my knees, letting the strings Wilson played until the knots in my soul and release me, even for a moment, from the burdens I dragged along like clanking cans and filthy chains. </i>
</b><br><br>Enter: Mr. Darcy Wilson, Blue’s hot, sophisticated, and very British history teacher. He’s a challenge for the easy Blue Echohawk. And she hates him. She hates his intensity, his ability to read people like a favorite book, and his questions.<br><br><b>
  <i> “What if what you believe about yourself or about your life is simply a myth that is holding you back?” </i>
</b><br><br>Until she loves him.<br><br>It’s a very slow and quiet love that begins out of respect, spins into friendship, and branches into love. <br><br>Wilson is that <i>one</i> person for Blue. He’s that person who teaches her to fly, to catch her when she’s in a tail-spin, and he’s that rock of a person for her to rest on. Wilson makes her want to be better.<br><br><b>
  <i> “There’s no sense in running from the past. We can’t throw it away or pretend it didn’t happen, Miss Echo hawk. But maybe we can learn something from it. You have an interesting story, and I’d like you to tell me more.” </i>
</b><br><br><i>MY REVIEW:</i><br><br>Amy Harmon does something extraordinary with this book. She doesn’t just tell a story; she makes you a part of it and let’s you in on the entire journey of building a story from the ground up only to watch her completely strip down its main character.<br><br>And it’s <b> awe-inspiring</b>.<br><br>“A Different Blue” isn’t your average action-packed romance novel with a lot of angst. It’s built on a more <i>emotional</i> foundation. <br><br>It’s a hurricane that hits you on a breeze. <br><br>And it <i>will</i> hit you.<br><br>I promise.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3981230311795557844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2218015648?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie Shores" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie Shores" href="/user/show/25177308-bonnie-shores">Bonnie Shores</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25177308-bonnie-shores?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2218015648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer737517110209356303"><i>Amazing grace, how sweet the sound that saved a wretch like me...</i><br/><br/>I didn't know what grace was, but maybe it sounded like the music. Maybe that was what I was feeling. <i>How sweet the sound.</i> And it was sweet, impossibly so. <i>How sweet the sound that saved a wretch like me.</i> Was a wretch the same thing as a bitch? Or a slut? My life was not a testament to being saved from anything. It was not a testament to love—not anybody's love.<br/><br/>My head firmly rejected the idea. Grace wouldn't save me. But in the ti</span>
  <span id="freeText737517110209356303" style="display:none"><i>Amazing grace, how sweet the sound that saved a wretch like me...</i><br><br>I didn't know what grace was, but maybe it sounded like the music. Maybe that was what I was feeling. <i>How sweet the sound.</i> And it was sweet, impossibly so. <i>How sweet the sound that saved a wretch like me.</i> Was a wretch the same thing as a bitch? Or a slut? My life was not a testament to being saved from anything. It was not a testament to love—not anybody's love.<br><br>My head firmly rejected the idea. Grace wouldn't save me. But in the tiny, neglected corner of my heart, freshly awakened by the music, I suddenly believed it might. I believed it could.<br><br><i>"God?"</i> I whispered, saying the name I'd never spoken except in profanity, not even once. But I'd sung his name once, long ago. The name felt sweet on my tongue, and I tasted it again. <i>"God?"</i> I waited. The music prodded me forward.<br><br><i>"God? I'm ugly inside. And it's not my fault. You know it's not. I'll take responsibility for some of it, but you've gotta own up to your part, too. Nobody saved me. Nobody gave a shit. Nobody came to my rescue."</i> I gulped, feeling the sorrow in my throat, making it hurt to swallow, but it was pain I'd been swallowing for a long time, and I forced it down. <i>"So I'm asking you now. Can you take it away? Can you take away the ugliness?"</i><br><br>Something broke inside of me, and I groaned, unable to bite it back. Hot wet shame flooded out of me in waves of crushing grief. I tried to speak, but the torrent was almost too much. And so I gasped the final plea.<br><br><i>"God? If you love me... take it away. Please. I'm asking you to take it away. I don't want to feel this way anymore."</i> I wrapped my head in my arms, and let the torrent consume me. I had never let myself cry like this. I had feared that if I opened the floodgates I would drown. But as the waves crashed over me, I was not consumed, I was swept up, washed, my soul blanketed with blessed relief. Hope rose within me like a buoy. And with the hope, came peace. And the peace calmed the waters and quieted the storm, until I sat, spent, bled out, done.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1513874554i/24731574.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I know this isn't a review, but my 5-star rating speaks to my love of this book. And the excerpt above spoke to me in a personal way and reminded me that God saved a wretch like me, too. <b>A Different Blue</b> is the story of one girl's “redemption, resolution, revelation, and relevance”.</span>
  <a data-text-id="737517110209356303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2453343289958313203">I know I have said this a few times lately however I think this is on of the best books of the year. It for sure ranks up there in the top 10 for me and I have read over 100 books this year more like 125. I am honestly taken by surprise by how much I liked this book. It was a very clean book no bad words and no sex although sex was talked about. It was a ya book which I don't typically read I prefer smut and lots of it. Honestly though this book is so good that is didn't need those other element</span>
  <span id="freeText2453343289958313203" style="display:none">I know I have said this a few times lately however I think this is on of the best books of the year. It for sure ranks up there in the top 10 for me and I have read over 100 books this year more like 125. I am honestly taken by surprise by how much I liked this book. It was a very clean book no bad words and no sex although sex was talked about. It was a ya book which I don't typically read I prefer smut and lots of it. Honestly though this book is so good that is didn't need those other elements it was beauty all on its on. It is truly a brilliant story and a unique one. I really enjoyed the direction this book took. I know some have considered it taboo but truly it isn't. The relationship between Blue and Wilson does not start until after she has graduated high school. It is a beautiful story!! I will be thinking of it a long time to come for sure. A must read people!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FQ9/O4gC3n0ihw0Gf+8c/hbg//mcKio/jgYJsns4j4K0eOB3MqRE4S9PVxhoONCoKCE7QC4l+qeIJHTGzS9Q8A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

<span id="freeTextContainer8343357436165782398">Amy Harmon is a Wall Street Journal, USA Today, and New York Times Bestselling author. Amy knew at an early age that writing was something she wanted to do, and she divided her time between writing songs and stories as she grew. Having grown up in the middle of wheat fields without a television, with only her books and her siblings to entertain her, she developed a strong sense of what made a good</span>
  <span id="freeText8343357436165782398" style="display:none">Amy Harmon is a Wall Street Journal, USA Today, and New York Times Bestselling author. Amy knew at an early age that writing was something she wanted to do, and she divided her time between writing songs and stories as she grew. Having grown up in the middle of wheat fields without a television, with only her books and her siblings to entertain her, she developed a strong sense of what made a good story. Her books are now being published in eighteen languages, truly a dream come true for a little country girl from Levan, Utah.<br /><br />Amy Harmon has written fifteen novels including the USA Today Bestsellers, Making Faces and Running Barefoot, as well as The Law of Moses, Infinity + One and the New York Times Bestseller, A Different Blue. Her fantasy novel, The Bird and the Sword, was a Goodreads Book of the Year finalist. Her newest release, What the Wind Knows, is an Amazon charts bestseller. For updates on upcoming book releases, author posts and more, join Amy at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.authoramyharmon.com">www.authoramyharmon.com</a>.</span>
